Peiris) There is nothing in that Motion to say - ගරු ලක්ෂ්මන් කිරිඇල්ල මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு லῆமன் கிாிஎல்ல) (The Hon. Lakshman Kiriella) But, if you read between the lines, it is very clear. The entire Opposition is hoping that; මුළු විපක්ෂයම පාර්ථනා කරනවා, එල්ටීටීඊ එක නැවත වරක් ඇති ෙව්වා-

ගරු මංගල සමරවීර මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு மங்கள சமரᾪர) (The Hon. Mangala Samaraweera) Hon. (Prof.) G.L. Peiris, never mind what you said, but the Member who seconded your Motion made it very clear as to what the intention of the Motion is. You may not have said it. ගරු ලක්ෂ්මන් කිරිඇල්ල මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு லῆமன் கிாிஎல்ல) (The Hon. Lakshman Kiriella) ගරු ඇමතිතුමා, එල්ටීටීඊ තස්තවාදින් පුනරුත්ථාපනය කරන්න බැරිද? බැරිද? 1988-1989 කාලෙය් ෙපොලීසිෙය් හා හමුදාෙව් සිය ගණනක් මරපු ඒවා ගැන දැන් ෙම් ගරු සභාෙව් කථා කරනවාද?

ඒ අයත් පුනරුත්ථාපනය ෙවලා. අද ෙම් පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුෙව් කථා කරපු අයත් 1988 හා 89 කාලෙය් සිය ගණනක් මැරුවා. අපි නම් ෙපොලීසිෙය් හමුදාෙව් අය මැරුෙව් නැහැ. ඒ ෙගොල්ෙලොත් පුනරුත්ථාපනය ෙවලා. පුනරුත්ථාපනය ෙවලා දැන් ෙමතැන කථා කරන්ෙන්. ඒ ෙගොල්ෙලෝ තමයි ෙලොකුම ෙද්ශෙපේමීන්. මූලාසනාරූඪ මන්තීතුමිය (தைலைமதாங்கும் உᾠப்பினர் அவர்கள்) (The Presiding Member) ගරු ඇමතිතුමා, ඔබතුමාට ෙවන් කළ කාලය අවසානයි. ගරු ලක්ෂ්මන් කිරිඇල්ල මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு லῆமன் கிாிஎல்ல) (The Hon. Lakshman Kiriella) එල්ටීටීඊ තස්තවාදීන්ව පුනරුත්ථාපනය කරන්න පුළුවන්.

මම අවසාන වශෙයන් එක කාරණයක් කියන්නම්. අද උතුරු නැ ෙඟනහිර ජනතාව බලා ෙගන ඉන්ෙන් මධɕම ආණ්ඩුවත් එක්ක එකට වැඩ කරන්නයි. ඒ අයට යුද්ධ කරලා එපා ෙවලා. අභɕන්තර පරීක්ෂණය ගැන අනිවාර්යෙයන්ම මංගල සමරවීර ඇමතිතුමා පකාශ කරයි. ජී.එල්. පීරිස් මන්තීතුමාට මා කියන්ෙන්, ෙම් වාෙග් ෙබෙදන්ෙන් නැතුව රට ෙවනුෙවන් ඔබතුමන්ලාෙග් සහෙයෝගය අපට ෙදන්න කියලායි. රට ෙවනුෙවන් සහෙයෝගය ෙදන්න. මට නියමිත කාලය අවසන් නිසා මෙග් කථාව අවසන් කරනවා. මූලාසනාරූඪ මන්තීතුමිය (தைலைமதாங்கும் உᾠப்பினர் அவர்கள்) (The Presiding Member) ෙබොෙහොම ස්තුතියි.

ඊළඟට ගරු (මහාචාර්ය) රාජීව විෙජ්සිංහ මන්තීතුමා. [5.18 p.m.] ගරු (මහාචාර්ය) රාජීව විෙජ්සිංහ මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு (ேபராசிாியர்) ராஜீவ விேஜசிங்க) (The Hon. (Prof.) Rajiva Wijesinha) Madam Chair, I am glad that this topic is being discussed through an Adjournment Motion since I really fear that the antics of this Government are taking us into grave danger. I feel the more worried about this because I was one of those who wanted a "change" at the last Presidential Election. As I made clear at the time, I felt that this was necessary if all of us - by "all of us", I mean

433 434

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව

also the Tamil and Muslim communities that had suffered so much from terrorism - were to benefit fully from the victory over the LTTE that we achieved in 2009.

I wonder, sometimes, if I should feel guilty about having, in a small way, promoted change, but on balance, I think it was clear that the last Government had begun to lose its way in the last few years and was no longer capable of fulfilling the pledges in its Election Manifesto of 2010. And, no one could have anticipated the contempt with which decision-makers in this Government treated their election pledges and the need for full reintegration of those who suffered in the war.

However, I think there is now a silver lining of sorts in that His Excellency the President, whose own commitment to his pledges seems absolute, as well as to the vision of this country that led to the victory of 2009, has begun to realize that some changes in the structure of authority are essential if we are not to collapse again, as we did so spectacularly under some of our previous leaders. In particular, I believe he understands that blind emulation of the foreign policy of J.R. Jayewardene will lead to similar disasters as occurred in the '80s and I am very pleased that the Front Bench of the Government is now full of former Members of the SLFP or people like the Hon. Karu Jayasuriya, who supported the victory against the LTTE because they understand what the root causes of that were and I will speak more about that.

However, it seems that the present Minister, despite his background, believes in putting all his eggs into a western basket. This was done by President Jayewardene in the '80s, only to find them taken out again and collectively smashed. In those days, his predilections included hostility to India, which he thought would be fulfilled by cosying up to the West in those Cold War days. But, for obvious reasons, the West did not save him and indeed, I believe he had been advised as such, but ignored the advice and that is why he sent off his Foreign Minister, the Hon. A.C.S. Hameed, to invoke the 1940s Defence Treaty with Britain, only to be politely told that that was not possible.

I do not think this Government will be contemptuous of India for philosophical reasons, but it seems that personal animosities could contribute to similar results. The decision to recall our current High Commissioner in India, one of the most imaginative and knowledgeable to serve there, simply because he was appointed by the last Government, is deeply depressing. There seems absolutely no regard for influential opinion in India which has queried whether a friend of India is being withdrawn. But, let us hope that intentions at least are sound with regard to India even though the blundering continues.

The same cannot be said of what has happened with regard to China, where the blunderbuss approach of the Government may well lead to problems. Only last week we had a report on what the Foreign Minister had said, after which a clarification had to be made, which turned

that Statement upside down. We have already had the Prime Minister attacking Australian policies simply because Australia did not do as he wanted with regard to the Commonwealth Heads of Government Meeting. Now, to attack, or create the impression of attacking, a country that has stood by us consistently seems midsummer madness.

Underlying this is a basic simplicity, and I saw as much in the speech of the very able Deputy Foreign Minister, that does not recognize the realities of foreign policy development in other countries. It is for this reason that I welcome the mention in this Motion of the Statement by Senator Patrick Leahy. Such a Statement could well be a precursor to a very hard line, and in particular we have to remember that next year is an election year in the United States when the funding capacity of the TGTE is massive and I fear very much that a harder and harder line will be pressed unless we move very swiftly towards a sensible resolution.

Meanwhile, the Foreign Minister dances with the GTF, which I do not think is bad in itself, but that is not where he should concentrate. Way back in 2009, on the last occasion when I had an executive position as the Head of the Sri Lanka Peace Secretariat, I was told by the Foreign Ministry in London that we should be talking to the Tamils and I said, "Of course, we should be talking to the Tamils. We won this war as much on behalf of the Tamils as the rest of this country" and they said, “Yes, you must talk to the TNA and the GTF. I said, “How dare you come out with such statements!". I think we should talk to the TNA, the TNA listens perfectly well, this is the stance I have always stood by, but I said that I do not believe we should be told to talk to people who were supporters of terrorism actively. It is the people of Sri Lanka we should be talking to and I do not think that we should dance to the tune of the international community that itself sometimes has to dance to the tune of a diaspora that still has very bitter memories. I can understand why they have bitter memories and I would like to come to that as well, but we cannot run a country on the basis of bitterness.

So, work with the diaspora is essential, more essential is working with those who have suffered in Sri Lanka. I know that reconciliation has been entrusted to the Foreign Minister's former leader and new best friend of the Prime Minister. But, there has been so little done in five months that I can understand why dissatisfaction is growing, and why perhaps the LTTE will find it easier and easier to renew its efforts at terrorism and separation.

Now, I believe, listening to the speeches that have gone before, it is necessary as they have indicated, to look a little bit of the history. I think, in particular, we have to recognize that following the victory of 2009, the last Government did not do many things that it should have done. Although, I was in the forefront of those who kept pressing it and it was all very clearly put forward: the need for an internal inquiry, rapid need, the need for better resettlement, the need for more consultation, I can also understand though I criticized it, the failure of the

435 436

[ගරු (මහාචාර්ය) රාජීව විෙජ්සිංහ මහතා]

2015 ජුනි 25

Government to move and that had to do with the deep suspicions that have become endemic in this country and for which there is good reason even though I believe we should overcome them. For instance, the distinguished Leader of the TNA is perfectly correct in saying that we should have done more during the negotiations. But, I also think he cannot forget his own admittedly enforced allegiance to the LTTE in the past. I remember, he referred to the discussions that led to what he termed the “G.L.Peiris-Neelan Tiruchelvam Agreement” and he should not forget the way that Agreement was betrayed and I always was very critical of him. But, he revealed to me three years ago that he had wanted to stand by that commitment, but he had been pushed out of his position by other Members of his party who were in turn under pressure from the LTTE. We know perfectly well that the UNP burnt that Agreement on the Floor of this House and the former President who was under the impression that she had secured the support of both the UNP and the LTTE for the proposal she put forward in 2010, found herself caught in a pincer movement by what seemed extremist Sinhala and extremist Tamil opinion and had to abandon that and I do not think it is correct of the Hon. Sampanthan to only criticize some of those who supported that Agreement then - but, do not mention it now - because his own role was also rather sad.

Similarly, I think we have to remember the claims of the TNA that the LTTE was the sole representative of the people and that is why we missed so much a man of courage like Neelan Tiruchelvam, who stood up against the LTTE. I do not condemn the Hon. Sampanthan because obviously he did not want to face the fate that Neelan Tiruchelvam faced. You know we are sad of Neelan's loss, but we have to remember the domination of the Tamil polity by the LTTE during those years and the way the perfectly-reasonable efforts that were moving forward were stymied.

Similarly, although I do not think it is correct of the last Government not to have done more, I also understand some of its diffidence and, in particular, the way in which the LLRC was treated has been very worrying. I know that when the Government appointed its own LLRC, later than it should have, there was much assumption that it would produce a partisan report. It produced a very good report which was welcomed by everybody, except three public commentaries, one of which was the TNA. The TNA’s statement at the time, similar to one by the CPA and another one by the US State Department - not the then Ambassador here - was so critical of the LLRC Report. That, I can understand though I think it was wrong, for the Government also which had tabled that Report to have not implemented it fully, because once you start pulling on to one side, then people on the other side start pulling as well. But, despite that, the LLRC Report developed into an Action Plan. That Action Plan was entrusted to some people who did nothing about it, who are now in positions of great authority, but the Secretary to the President took charge, produced an excellent Action Plan. It had some shortcomings but, at

least, some things went forward. Now, that has been completely forgotten. I was in touch with those who were implementing the Action Plan and I had to speak regularly to the UN and the international community. They were surprised that there is no mention whatsoever of the LLRC and the work it has done in whatever the proposals are, that the committees under the chairmanship of the former President are doing. I think we cannot keep reinventing the wheel. The LLRC, the people who worked on it - the very distinguished Deputy Head was sent into the pool, but I think he is now being rescued - cannot be just cast aside because they worked for the last Government. And, it seems to me tragic that we took so very long to move on reconciliation. It was so, too, with the diaspora. In January or February, there was a continuation of an initiative that I had started many years back to work with young members of the diaspora. They were very positive. But, they felt that they were treated with contempt because all that they were told was investment. They are not cash cows.

I had actually put forward a paper in my brief tenure as a State Minister about using the services of the diaspora that has been completely forgotten. Young people also want to get involved; they do not want to be treated as people who just bring in money. They can help us with education. Many of them did so in small initiatives that I had started as adviser on reconciliation. We should build on those. I sent the former President a copy of the National Reconciliation Policy that was drafted with the support of, I think, the finest minds in the TNA and the UNP. I was very sorry the last Government did not adopt that. And, I got a reply which said, “Yes there are some good ideas here; we will think about them” and I am astonished that you thought the former President was interested. I mean, scoring debating points on such serious issues is not what we should be doing. That reconciliation policy has a lot to recommend it but by all means, amend it as you wish. But, for God's sake draft and put in place a reconciliation policy soon.

Similarly, we talked about an internal inquiry. I said I was one of those who kept wanting an internal inquiry for many years, I kept recommending it. But, I could understand, though I disagreed, with the philosophy of the last Government who felt beleaguered and threatened and felt that whatever they did would be used against it. I still remember, when I first mentioned the number of casualties, I was attacked by the then Attorney-General who said that the Defence Secretary was very angry with me for giving the figure and he said, “Why did you do this?” I said, “Because it was true. There were a number of figures and that is what we finally think is correct". Then he said, “They will use it.” And, I realized that this was the case because when I said this on “Hard Talk”, the answer was, “So, you admit”. Unfortunately, there are not many people who know how to deal with that. They either say, “Yes” or “No”. But, the answer is very clear. Saying that there were civilian casualties is not saying

437 438

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව

that they were inflicted deliberately, and all the evidence we have is during the conduct of the war, we did our best to fight it decently.

I, myself, have written about the need for inquiries as the LLRC had about what happened after the war and I think there is a prima facie case to be looked at and that is what our internal inquiry should be about. But, why has this not happened for five months? In February, when I was a Member of the Government Parliamentary Group, I said,“Publish the findings of the Udalagama Commission” because there are complaints that our Commissions are not to be trusted. The Udalagama Commission Report, as far as I know, is a very clear document that addresses issues in a way that everyone can accept; it was agreed at the Government Parliamentary Group. The following month, when I went back it was not even minuted. All that was in the minute was how to get cars for MPs and how to find jobs. The Hon. Deputy Minister of Foreign Affairs had raised the question publicly, because he said all his supporters wanted jobs and it was minuted. But, the important things were not minuted. The decisions made with regard to promoting good governance and the subcommittee established under the Minister, who has unfortunately now forgotten his responsibilities in that regard for reasons he has explained, but it is a pity. The decision to publish it was not done and when I asked the Hon. Prime Minister he told the Chief Government Whip, “Please incorporate this in the minutes” and he said he had not had time to look into this, but he would. Nothing has happened and the internationals we talk to said, "This is the type of thing you should be doing. It shows the bona fides". As I said, I can understand, though I regret why the last Government did not publish that, because I believe it is very clear about the need for prosecution in particular of those who killed the "Trinco five". But, as we know, that was an appalling action. It was not done by the armed forces and one of the reasons I was very angry with the last Government for not pursuing that, was by allowing such things to happen they allowed blanket accusations against the army, which as we know, did its best and we also know perfectly well that in the whole campaign in the Eastern Province before the LTTE perfected in its technique of hostage taking, there was only one allegation of civilians being killed and that was well explained by the army. So, these are areas in which we have things that can be answered and it is a great pity that the Government has spent five months doing nothing in this regard. I am very happy that the Minister of Foreign Affairs has now taken upon himself to work on these. I hope he will succeed, but I think the lack of action so far makes me fear the worst.

Finally, Madam Chair, I think we also need to look at what I can only describe as "a mixing of issues", which I hope the Leader of the TNA will also take seriously. I am

sorry that two times my Question was not answered, perhaps because I was present and the Foreign Minister was not; a couple of weeks were asked for that. But, my Question with regard to Ms. Tamara Kunanayakam was answered two Fridays ago when I was away. I am sorry I was not here. But, I was horrified by the answer because that answer is precisely what the Hon. Lakshman Kiriella condemned, this whole idea of LTTE-ising, and what the Minister of Foreign Affairs omitted to say, which I found very shabby, is that the representations made by Ms. Kunanayakam on behalf of a group that was led at the time by Kumar Rupesinghe, was with regard to the events of July 1983, and I hope that you will not believe that people who criticized what happened in 1983 are wrong because we know there were appalling things that happened. We know that the LTTE developed because of what the then Government unleashed in 1983. We know perfectly well that in 1981, when the LTTE wanted the District Development Council elections boycotted, the TULF was able to stand up against it and because of what happened a few months later, in 1982 the TULF had to give in to the LTTE with regard to elections - the burning of the Jaffna Public Library - but, nothing compared with what happened in 1983. And, when the Hon. R. Sampanthan talks about the people fleeing, I can understand why they left.

Yesterday, there was a speech in which it was claimed, I think, by the Hon. Minister of Justice that the Sixth Amendment was introduced in order to stop separatism. He forgot that the reaction of the UNP Government in 1983 to the appalling attacks on Tamils was to introduce this Sixth Amendment on the claim that the government needed to appease the feeling of the Sinhalese who had attacked the Tamils.

That was a credibly shabby behaviour and I believe the Minister of Foreign Affairs - I do not know whether he was involved in politics at that time, we knew each other under different circumstances - knows that what happened in 1983 was appalling; I believe that the Leader of the House knows what happened in 1983 was appalling. And, to condemn Ms. Kunanayakam as an LTTE activist for her outlining of information with regard to that incident is an incredibly shabby behaviour and, I believe, it shows that the Minister of Foreign Affairs is subject to manipulation by the same individuals, who failed when they were entrusted with developing an Action Plan from the LLRC Report. He knows perfectly well that this had been entrusted to the Ministry of External Affairs mistakenly in 2012, and that nothing was done about it. It took Mr. Weeratunga, as I said, to produce an Action Plan.

So, I believe it is important, Madam Chair, if we are going to go back into history - and perhaps we need to go into history as a whole - to look at those people now on the Government side of the House who were responsible for what happened in July, 1983. All of you will recall

439 440

[ගරු (මහාචාර්ය) රාජීව විෙජ්සිංහ මහතා]

2015 ජුනි 25

that the Prime Minister, at that stage, mitigated what had been done by saying that what Tamils had suffered in the pogrom of 1983 was nothing like what Sinhala entrepreneurs had suffered because of the nationalization policies of the Bandaranaike regime and he claimed, he shed tears on behalf of ship chandlers, sand collectors et cetera, who he said, had suffered an economic deprivation because of the policies of nationalization and he tried to defend what had happened in July, 1983, which was appalling. I know that new allies may forget all that, but I know that the Tamil people are well aware of what was done then and, while I believe, that there is a very strong component of the UNP, I hope all those Members in the Front Bench are those whom I could say have no racism in them, but I think we have to recognize that there was a strong racist streak. I still remember that that particular wing was even talking then of Cyril Mathew being the next leader of the Government, and in such a context, I think we have to remember what happened and how the LTTE managed to emerge.

Now, we have an opportunity because we have a President, who is not racist, but stood firm with the last Government in its struggle against terrorism, did not belittle the achievements of the army like so many Members on that side of the House did, and he did not even try to stop the victorious march of the forces against terrorists. Now that we have a President who can balance the different requirements of this country, I do not see why we are not moving forward; I do not see why we are not setting in place the mechanism for good governance that would ensure proper consultation.

I have said previously that it is the people in the deprived areas who need to be consulted. I think part of the problem is that in Colombo, we either talk to the moderate Colombo Tamils - and there is good reason for that and I have the highest regard for people like the Hon. Sumanthiran as I did for Neelan Tiruchelvam - or we listen to what I call the "ideological extremists" in the North. There is a strong lobby there that has very, very strong feelings. But, what we are missing out on is the ordinary people, the people of the Vanni, the people in the pradeshiya sabhas and the people in the divisional secretariats. When I was the Adviser on Reconciliation, I helped to set up consultation mechanisms, which were working extremely well and, I am happy to say, what the people then told me is that I was the only person who came there. We were talked to about settlement in the North. I was the person who raised that question in the Ministry of Resettlement and I upgraded the present Minister who did not even bother to come and find out. I told him - I never imagined that he would soon be Minister himself because he knew nothing - “Mr. Swaminathan, you have to be here. You have to find out what is happening”.

It was because of me that the mice who are now roaring about electoral reform actually raised the issue of

settlement in the Northern Province. But, having said that, I think that the process of returning land in the North has been far too slow but even worse, there is no planning. When you are going to do resettlement, you have not only to resettle but you have to work on livelihoods. You cannot go around asking in a vague way as the Minister does, “Can I have some money to resettle people?” You must have a plan. You must think about employment opportunities, in particular, for women. All that is in our national reconciliation policy, just as it is hinted at in the very good Report of the UN Special Rapporteur on the Promotion of Truth, Justice, Reparation and Guarantees of Non-recurrence, Mr. Pablo de Greiff, who was here. We had not even replied to that document. I gather that the Head of the Reconciliation outfit, former President Kumaratunga, was not here to meet him and he was not able to meet the task force. He did meet the Chairman but the Chairman has now resigned. I believe, my old friend Mr. Maliyadda, is now Chairman. Much can be done, but if you start from scratch, you will not get very far.

Sir, it is absolutely essential to look at all the documentation: we have a Human Rights Action Plan, we have an LLRC Action Plan, we have a draft National Policy on Reconciliation done with full consultation. These should be the basis on future action. We cannot depend on ad hoc meetings in London with people from the GTF, who had a very different agenda in the past. I do not see any reason not to try to reclaim them, but why do we not actually work with those who were willing to work with us three years ago - the young people, the people in the North ? Why do we not actually set in place a consultative process instead of hugging things?

When I told the former President, “You should really be doing more”, he said “එක පශ්නයක් තිෙබනවා, හැෙමෝම තමන්ෙග් එක බදාෙගන ඉන්නවා.” Now, we have even more “බදාෙගන ඉන්නවාs” on the part of the Government. Indeed most of the “බදාෙගන” happens on the part of the Prime Minister, who will not allow capable people to move forward. So, Sir, this is a very timely motion. We have to remember that reconciliation must begin at home. We have recommendations in the LLRC that can easily be implemented. These should be taken forward with full consultation of those officials who have been involved in such matters in the past, and then in arranging our foreign policy, we have to engage in much deeper thinking. When I was helping to draft the manifesto, which has now been, I think, totally violated, we talked about a Professional Foreign Service. This was interpreted to me into as to call back everyone who was not a member of the Foreign Service except a few retired people and Mr. Gamini Rajapakse, former Member of Parliament in Jordan. But, now it has turned into call back everyone the last government appointed and not what should be the case, which I suggested in the papers I fleshed out and which I sent to the Minister of Public Administration, Local Government and Democratic Governance, how you

441 442

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව

actually have some clear criteria on making appointments, how you develop policy and how you improve your think tanks.

I just saw recently that the last Head of the Lakshman Kadirgamar Institute for International Relations and Strategic Studies has delivered a stalling account of the new favourite of the Minister of Foreign Affairs, Ms. Kshenuka Seneviratne, who had actually tried to stop him from interacting internationally and pushing a course of reconciliation when he delivered some papers and she had basically tried to get rid of him by trying to limit his freedom of expression.

There was an admirable reply that he sent, but this is the person who is now the flavour of the month of the Foreign Minister and has contributed to this outrageous attack on Tamara Kunanayakam. There is another situation where the Foreign Ministry’s spokesperson, my old friend and a very good Service Officer, Maheshini Colonne, has to do damage control all the time. The "Daily Mirror" had approached Tamara Kunanayakam as had the TNL, to ask why the Foreign Minister had said that they could not get hold of you. Later, when it was explained that she was in the country and was easily accessible, the Foreign Minister had to say, “No, we have never said anything of the sort”. Now, the real tragedy about all this is that we find personal vendettas are destroying the interests of this country. Tamara Kunanayakam had been appointed Chair of the Intergovernmental Working Group on the Right to Development and instructions were sent by this Government to stop her being re-appointed. Even the last Government which was very annoyed with her - rather some people in the Foreign Ministry - did not try to stop her. This time those instructions were sent and when I asked the Foreign Minister, he said that he did not know about this. But, the Finance Minister let the cat out of the bag by saying, "Why should he appoint her because she is trying to sue the Foreign Minister." Now, we find that this lady who did so much for the Non-Aligned Movement and was highly regarded has been removed and the UN Working Group on Enforced or Involuntary Disappearances, which the West did not particularly want to take forward is now stymied. Now, we are not here to actually follow a myopic foreign policy as happened in the '80s. I think what we want to do is, omnidirectional. "Omnidirectional" does not mean hitting out on all sides as seems to have been the case occasionally, in particular, for instance, the attack on Australia. But, I think what it means is, following the principles of Non-Alignment. If you look at the President’s Manifesto, this is what he said in the Manifesto, "To develop relations with Asian countries: India, China et cetera". This does not preclude improving relations with the West, which I think is very important. But, to imagine that this can be exclusive is extremely myopic. And, if you study history, - I am glad

so many people did talk about history - you will realize that in the last resort the West had its own predilections, the West had interest groups. People like Senator Leahy are going to be very, very important and that is why putting all your eggs into one basket will lead you having them smashed as happened to President Jayewardene and the Foreign Minister, Hameed, way back in 1983, 1984, 1985, 1986 and 1987.

Thank you. [අ.භා. 5.50] ගරු කරු ජයසූරිය මහතා (රාජɕ පරිපාලන, පළාත් පාලන හා පජාතාන්තීය පාලනය පිළිබඳ අමාතɕ සහ බුද්ධ ශාසන අමාතɕතුමා) (மாண்ᾗமிகு கᾞ ஜயசூாிய - ெபாᾐ நிᾞவாக, உள்ᾧராட்சி மற்ᾠம் சனநாயக ஆட்சி பற்றிய அைமச்சᾞம் ᾗத்த சாசன அைமச்சᾞம்) (The Hon. Karu Jayasuriya - Minister of Public Administration, Local Government and Democratic Governance and Minister of Buddha Sasana) මූලාසනාරූඪ ගරු මන්තීතුමියනි, මෙග් හිත මිත (මහාචාර්ය) රාජීව විෙජ්සිංහ මැතිතුමාෙගන් පස්ෙසේ කථා කිරීමට අවස්ථාව ලැබීම ගැන මා සන්ෙතෝෂ වනවා. විෙශේෂෙයන්ම එතුමාෙග් කථාෙව්දී උගත් පාඩම් හා පතිසන්ධානය පිළිබඳ වූ ජනාධිපති ෙකොමිෂන් සභාෙව් වාර්තාව ගැන ඉතාමත් වැදගත් අදහස් කීපයක් පළ වුණා.

මූලාසනාරූඪ ගරු මන්තීතුමියනි, මෙග් කථාව ආරම්භ කිරීමට පථමෙයන් මා කියන්න ඕනෑ, අපත් ෙම් රටට ආදරය කරන පුද්ගලයන් බව. ජාති හිෛතෂීන්, ෙද්ශ ෙපේමීන් කියා අප ෙබල්ෙල් ෙබෝඩ් එල්ලාෙගන හිටිෙය් නැති වුණාට අපත් ෙම් රටට ආදරය කරන පුද්ගලයන්. ඒ වාෙග්ම ෙම් රෙට් මිහිදන් වන පුද්ගලයන් ව ශෙයන් අපත් ෙම් රටට කිසිම විධියකින් හානියක් ෙවන්න ඉඩ ෙදන්ෙන් නැහැ. ඇෙමරිකා එක්සත් ජනපදෙය් රාජɕ ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුෙව් 2014 වාර්තාව ගැන කථා කිරීමට අවස්ථාව ලැබීම ගැන මා සන්ෙතෝෂ වනවා. කල් තැබීෙම් ෙයෝජනාවක් ඉදිරිපත් කර, ඒ ගැන සාකච්ඡා කිරීමට අවස්ථාවක් ලබා දීම සම්බන්ධෙයන් (මහාචාර්ය) ජී.එල්. පීරිස් මැතිතුමාට -එතුමා මෙග් මිතයා.- මා ස්තුතිවන්ත වනවා.

මූලාසනාරූඪ ගරු මන්තීතුමියනි, මා පළමුෙවන්ම කියන්න කැමැතියි, 2014 අවුරුද්ෙද්ත්, 2015 අවුරුද්ෙද්ත් යම් ෙවනස්වීමක් ඇති වුණු බව. 2005 සිට 2015 ජනවාරි 08 වැනිදා දක්වා එක් රජයක් තිබුණා. 2015 ජනවාරි 09 වැනිදායින් පස්ෙසේ අලුත් පාලනයක් ඇති වුණා. ඒ නිසා මට කියන්න පුළුවන්, නව පාලනය තුළ අප ෙම් රෙට් ජනතාවට පජාතන්තවාදය ස්ථාපිත කිරීමත්; මිනිස් අයිතිවාසිකම් ආරක්ෂා කර දීමත් වාෙග්ම ලිවීෙම් හා කථා කිරීෙම් නිදහසත් ලබා දුන් බව. විෙශේෂෙයන්ම උතුෙර් ජනතාවට බල පැවැත්වූ කරුණු කීපයක් සම්බන්ධෙයන් අවධානය ෙයොමු කර, උතුෙර්ත්, නැ ෙඟනහිරත් ජනතාවට ෙම් රෙට් ෙගෞරවනීය පුරවැසියන් වශෙයන් ජීවත් වීෙම් අවස්ථාව අප ලබා දුන්නා. මාර්ග බාධක අයින් කර ගමන් කිරීෙම් පහසුව, කථා කිරීෙම් නිදහස, අදහස් පකාශ කිරීෙම් නිදහස ආදී සියලුම ෙද් ෙම් සුළු කාලය තුළ ලබා දුන්නා. ඒ වාෙග්ම මා සඳහන් කරන්න ඕනෑ, ෙප බරවාරි 04 වැනිදා පැවති ජාතික නිදහස් දින උත්සවයට ෙදමළ ජාතික සන්ධානෙය් -TNA එෙක්- මන්තීවරුන් සහභාගී වුණු බව. එය විෙශේෂ අවස්ථාවක්. දශක කීපයකට පස්ෙසේ එතුමන්ලා එදා ජාතික නිදහස් දින උත්සවයට සහභාගී වීම තුළ

443 444

[ගරු (මහාචාර්ය) රාජීව විෙජ්සිංහ මහතා]

2015 ජුනි 25

අප අලුත් ෙවනසක් දුටුවා. ෙම් රෙට් ඉදිරි ගමෙන්දී අප ඔක්ෙකොටම මහජන නිෙයෝජිතයන් වශෙයන් එකට වැඩ කිරීෙම් බලාෙපොෙරොත්තුව සහ ඒ විශ්වාසය එදා ෙපන්වා දුන්නා. නව රජය බලයට පත් වුණාට පස්ෙසේ විෂයය භාර අමාතɕවරයා වශෙයන් මා තුන් හතර වතාවක් උතුෙර් සංචාරය කළ බව මට මතකයි. උතුරු පළාත් සභාෙව් පධාන අමාතɕතුමා වාෙග්ම ගරු මන්තීතුමන්ලා මා සමග සහභාගී වුණා. ඒ අයට තිබුණු ෙබොෙහෝ ගැටලු විසඳා ෙදන්න අපට පුළුවන් වුණා. ඒ අයට අවශɕ යන්තසූත, මුදල්, යාන වාහන ලබා ෙදන්න හැකි වුණා. ෙබොෙහෝ කාලයක් ඒ පාලනයට බාධා පැමිණුනා. පත් වුණු නිලධාරින් නිසා බාධා පැමිණුනා. ඒ වාෙග්ම පරිපාලනෙය් සිටි අයෙගන් බාධා පැමිණුනා. එතුමා එක් අවස්ථා වක සඳහන් කළා, එතුමා ෙදන සමහර නිෙයෝග කනිෂ්ඨ ෙසේවකයා පවා පිළිගත්ෙත් නැහැ කියා. එවැනි තත්ත්වයක් තිබුණා. අප ඒ තත්ත්වය ෙවනස් කළා. ඒ වාෙග්ම මා ෙම් අවස්ථාෙව්දී සඳහන් කරන්න ඕනෑ, ෙකොටි සංවිධානයට අන්තර්ජාතිකව බලපෑම් කරන්නට බැරි තත්ත්වයක් අද ඇති ෙවලා තිෙබන බව.

මා විෙශේෂෙයන් සඳහන් කරන්න ඕනෑ, අෙප් නව විෙද්ශ පතිපත්තිය තුළ ගරු ජනාධිපතිතුමා වාෙග්ම ගරු අගාමාතɕතුමා ෙලෝක පජාෙව් ෙගෞරවයට පාත වූ පුද්ගලයන් ෙදෙදෙනක් බව. අතිගරු ජනාධිපතිතුමා සංචාරය කළ සෑම රටකින්ම අෙප් රටට ලැබුණු පතිචාර අප දැක්කා. මහ රැජිනෙග් සිට චීන ජනාධිපති, ඉන්දියන් ජනපති වාෙග්ම සංචාරය කළ සෑම රටකින්ම ලංකාව ෙකෙරහි අලුත් ආකල්පයක් ඇති වනවා අප දුටුවා.

මා ෙම් අවස්ථාෙව්දී සඳහන් කරන්ෙන් අෙප් විෙද්ශ කටයුතු අමාතɕතුමා විෙද්ශ කටයුතු අමාතɕාංශෙය් විශාල ෙවනසක් ඇති කළ බවයි. එතුමා විෙද්ශ කටයුතු අමාතɕාංශෙය් කාර්යක්ෂතාව වැඩි කළා. ඒ වාෙග්ම එතුමා සංචාරය කළ සෑම රටකම ලංකාවට වාසි වන විධියට ලංකාෙව් ෙගෞරවය, ලංකාෙව් කීර්තිය ස්ථාපිත කරන්නට එතුමාට හැකි වුණු බව අපි දුටුවා. ඒ ගමනින් පස්ෙසේ අපත් හඳුනන, අපත් සමඟ ආශය කරන සමහර විෙද්ශීය අමාතɕවරු ෙබොෙහෝ ෙදෙනක් ඒ ගැන අපට සඳහන් කර තිබුණා. අද ෙලෝකෙය් ෙබොෙහෝ රටවල් ලංකාව දිහා බලන්ෙන් අමුතු ඇහැකින්. අද විෙද්ශ කටයුතු අමාතɕාංශයට දක්ෂ නිලධාරින් පත් කර ෙම් රෙට් යථා තත්ත්වය ෙලෝකයට ෙපන්වා දීමට කටයුතු කර තිෙබනවා.

විෙශේෂෙයන්ම ඩයස්ෙපෝරාව ගැන කථා කරනෙකොට ෙම් කාරණයත් කියන්න ඕනෑ. ඩයස්ෙපෝරාව කියන්ෙන් ෙකොටි හමුදාවක්, විෙද්ශෙය් ඉන්න දවිඩ ෙකොටි පිරිසක් පමණයි කියා අවාසනාවකට ෙම් රෙට් මතයක් ඇති ෙවලා තිෙබනවා. මූලාසනාරූඪ ගරු මන්තීතුමියනි, ෙමහිදී ඩයස්ෙපෝරාව කියන්ෙන් විෙද්ශෙය් ඉන්න විවිධ ජාතින්ටයි. ඒ ඩයස්ෙපෝරාවට සිංහලයන් ෙබොෙහෝ පිරිසක් සිටිනවා; මුස්ලිම් අය ෙබොෙහෝ පිරිසක් සිටිනවා; දවිඩ ජනතාව සිටිනවා. ෙම් සියලු ෙදනාම තස්තවාදය අනුමත කරන අය ෙනොෙවයි. ඒ වාෙග්ම මා ආඩම්බර ෙවනවා, විෙද්ශීය ඩයස්ෙපෝරාෙව් අෙප් ෙකෝටිපතියන්, පෙකෝටිපතියන්, billionaireලා ඉන්න එක ගැන. ඇෙමරිකාෙව් නාසා ආයතනෙය් ඉන්න විෙශේෂඥයන් ෙබොෙහෝ ෙදෙනක් ලංකාෙව් අය, ෙබොෙහෝ ෙදෙනක් සිංහල අය. ඒ වාෙග්ම දවිඩ අයත් සිටිනවා. එක්සත් ජාතින්ෙග් සංවිධානෙය් වියානා පධාන කාර්යාලෙය් සිටින නිලධාරින්ෙගන් ෙබොෙහෝ ෙදෙනක් ලංකාෙව් අය. අද ෙම් ඩයස්ෙපෝරාව, අෙප් රෙට් ජනතාව ෙලෝකෙය් සෑම තැනකදීම ෙගෞරවයට පාත ෙවලා තිෙබනවා. ලංකාෙව් කීර්තිමත් විනිශ්චයකාරවරුන්, කීර්තිමත් Attorney-Generalවරුන් අද ෙලෝකෙය් ෙබොෙහෝ රටවල ෙසේවය කරනවා. ඒ අය ලංකාව

ෙකෙරහි විශාල ෙගෞරවයක් ලබා ෙදනවා. සිංහල ෙව්වා, දවිඩ ෙව්වා, මුස්ලිම් ෙව්වා අද ෙම් අය ලංකාවට ඒ ෙගෞරවය ලබා දීලා තිෙබනවා.

ගරු විෙද්ශ කටයුතු අමාතɕතුමා ෙම් සම්බන්ධෙයන් ෙයෝජනා ඉදිරිපත් කළ යුතු අවස්ථාෙව්දී අපි සන්ෙතෝෂ වුණා. ඒක ඉන්දියාෙව් අගමැති ෙමෝදි මැතිතුමා ෙබොෙහොම කාර්යක්ෂම ෙලස කළා. අද ඉන්දියාෙව් සංවර්ධනය සඳහා ඉන්දියානු ඩයස්ෙපෝරාෙව් විශාල සංඛɕාවක් ආපසු එන්න පටන් ෙගන තිෙබනවා. ඒ වාෙග් අද ලංකාෙව් අෙප් පතිපත්තීන් තුළ, අපි ඇති කර තිෙබන ෙම් වාතාවරණය තුළ ඒ ඩයස්ෙපෝරාවට ලංකාවට ඇවිල්ලා සංවර්ධන කටයුතුවලට ෙකළින්ම සහභාගි ෙවන්න පුළුවන්. ඒ අයට අතිවිශාල මුදල් සම්භාරයක් තිෙබන බව මා දන්නවා. ඒකයි, මා සඳහන් කෙළේ, millionaireලා කිව්වාම රුපියල් millionaireලා ෙනොෙවයි, ෙඩොලර් millionaireලා, billionairලා, පවුම් millionaireලා, billionaireලා සිටිනවා, සිංහල අය සිටිනවා, දවිඩ අය සිටිනවා, මුස්ලිම් අය සිටිනවාය කියා. මා ඒ අය ගැන ආඩම්බර වනවා. අද ෙලෝකෙය් ෙබොෙහෝ රටවල, විෙශේෂෙයන්ම එංගලන්තෙය්, ඇෙමරිකාෙව්, යුෙරෝපෙය්, ජර්මනිෙය් එවැනි අය සිටිනවා. ඒ අය ලංකාවට ෙගන්වා ගැනීෙම්දී කිසිම විධියක හානියක් අපට ෙවයි කියා මා දකින්ෙන් නැහැ. මා එතුමාට ශුභ පාර්ථනා කරනවා. ෙදසැම්බරෙය් එතුමා බලාෙපොෙරොත්තු වන ඒ සංවර්ධනය තුළින් ෙම් රෙට් ෙවනසක් ඇති ෙවන්න පුළුවන්. ෙමෝදි අගාමාතɕතුමා ගත් කියාදාමය අනුගමනය කිරීම ඉතාමත් වැදගත් පියවරක් වශෙයන් මා දකිනවා. ෙමතැනදී මා ෙපෞද්ගලිකව ඒ ගැන කලබල වන්ෙන් නැහැ. කලබල ෙනොෙවන්න ෙහේතුවක් තිෙබනවා. ඒ වාෙග්ම අෙප් පතිපත්තිවල කිසිම ෙවනසක් ඇති ෙවලා නැහැ. ෙමොකද, අපි එදා කිව්වා වාෙග් අනාගතෙය්දීත් කියන්ෙන් අන්තර්ජාතික පරීක්ෂණයකට අෙප් රජය අපි එකඟ වන්ෙන් නැහැ කියායි. අන්තර්ජාතික පරීක්ෂණයක් අවශɕ නැති බව අපි මුල ඉඳලාම කියපු ෙදයක් තමයි. එම නිසා ෙද්ශීය පරීක්ෂණයක් ගැන තමයි අපි කථා කරන්ෙන්. අපි ඒ මතෙය් දැඩිව ඉන්නවා.

තවත් ෙදයක් කියන්න ඕනෑ. Senator Patrick Leahy සඳහන් කරපු ෙද් එතුමාෙග් ෙපෞද්ගලික මතය ෙවන්න පුළුවන්. ෙකොපමණ බලගතු ෙකනකු වුණත් ඒ සඳහන් කරපු ෙද් ෙකෙරහි අපට ඕනෑවට වඩා කලබල ෙවන්න ෙහේතුවක් නැහැ. එම නිසා ඒ ගැන අපි කලබල වන්ෙන් නැහැ. නමුත් ෙමතැනදී මා එකක් කියන්න ඕනෑ. ෙම් රෙට් වර්තමාන රජය නැවතත් ෙම් රෙට් තස්තවාදය ඇති වීමට කිසිම විධියකින් ඉඩක් ෙදන්ෙන් නැහැ. ෙලෝකෙය් ඉහළම මට්ටෙමන් මැනිය හැකි, ඒ වාෙග්ම පිළිගත හැකි සන්නද්ධ හමුදා ශක්තියක් ෙම් රෙට් තිෙබනවා. ඒ වාෙග්ම විනය ගරුක, එඩිතර, කාර්ය ශූර හමුදා ශක්තියක් අපට තිෙබනවා. අපි දන්නවා, අද ෙලෝක පජාවෙග් ෙගෞරවය ඔවුන්ට ලැබී තිෙබන බව. ඒ වාෙග්ම ජාතික සමඟිය ඇති කිරීම සඳහා සිංහල, දවිඩ, මුස්ලිම් ආදී සෑම ෙකොටස් සමඟම අපි -වර්තමාන රජය- කිට්ටුෙවන් වැඩ කරනවා.

උතුෙර්දී සම්පන්දන් නායකතුමාට අපට කථා කරන්න පුළුවන්. ඒ පක්ෂෙය් නායකයන්ට අපට කථා කරන්න පුළුවන්. නැ ෙඟනහිර මුස්ලිම් නායකයන්ට අපට කථා කරන්න පුළුවන්. ෙම් රෙට් දැෙවන පශ්න ගැන අපට එකට ඉඳ ෙගන කථා කරන්න පුළුවන්. අන්න ඒ විශ්වාසය ෙම් නව රජය විසින් ඇති කර ෙගන තිෙබන බව සඳහන් කරමින්, මට ෙම් අවස්ථාව ලබා දීම ගැන ඔබතුමියට ස්තුතිවන්ත ෙවමින් මාෙග් වචන ස්වල්පය අවසන් කරනවා.

445 446

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව

[අ.භා. 6.00] ගරු මංගල සමරවීර මහතා (විෙද්ශ කටයුතු අමාතɕතුමා) (மாண்ᾗமிகு மங்கள சமரᾪர - ெவளிநாட்டᾤவல்கள் அைமச்சர்) (The Hon. Mangala Samaraweera - Minister of Foreign Affairs) මූලාසනෙයන් අවසරයි. හිටපු විෙද්ශ ඇමති මහාචාර්ය ජී.එල්. පීරිස් මැතිතුමා විසින් අද ෙගන එන ලද ඒ වාෙග්ම විමල් වීරවංශ මන්තීවරයා විසින් ස්ථිර කරන ලද ෙමම ෙයෝජනාව සම්බන්ධෙයන් මාෙග් අදහස් දක්වන්නට අවස්ථාවක් ලැබීම ගැන මා සතුටු ෙවනවා. ඇත්ත වශෙයන්ම ෙම් ෙයෝජනාව ෙගන එමින් ජී.එල්. පීරිස් මන්තීතුමා සමබර, වැදගත් අදහස් රාශියක් ඉදිරිපත් කළත්, ෙම් ෙයෝජනාෙව් සැබෑ අරමුණ, -ෙම් ෙයෝජනාෙව් සැබෑ උවමනාව- ෙම් ෙයෝජනාව ස්ථිර කළ මන්තීවරයාෙග් කථාෙවන් පැහැදිලි වුණා. අද ෙම් ෙයෝජනාෙව් අපි කථා කරන කාරණා සම්බන්ධෙයන් එතුමා පමණක් ෙනොෙවයි, පසු ගිය දින කිහිපය තුළදී ශී ලංකා නිදහස් පක්ෂෙය් අභයාරාම පාර්ශ්වය විසින් ඉදිරිපත් කරන ලද අදහස් දිහා බැලුවාමත් මට අද විපක්ෂෙය් එම කණ්ඩායෙම් තිෙබන "හක්ෙක් බුදුරැස්, ෙබොක්ෙක් දඩමස්" පතිපත්තිය ෙහොඳින් ෙපනුණා. මම හිතන විධියට අෙප් දිෙන්ෂ් ගුණවර්ධන මැතිතුමා අද ෙම් අවස්ථාෙව්දී කථා කරන්න ඉඳලාත් නිහඬ වුෙණ් එතුමාත් ෙමය ෙත්රුම් ගත් නිසා ෙවන්න ඇති.

අද අෙප් ආණ්ඩුවට, මට, අෙප් අමාතɕාංශයට විවිධාකාර අභූත ෙචෝදනා නඟන ෙකොටස් පසු ගිය කාලෙය්දී පසු ගිය රජය ෙම් ආකාරයටම යම් යම් අවස්ථාවල කටයුතු කරන ෙකොට ඒ ගැන නිහඬව සිටියා. දැන් ෙම් ඩයස්ෙපෝරා කථාව තමයි රෙට් ඉස්මතු ෙවලා තිෙබන්ෙන්. ෙමොකද, මම මීට සති ෙදකකට විතර ඉස්සර ෙවලා කිව්වා, ඩයස්ෙපෝරා උෙළලක් තිෙබනවා කියලා. ඒක කිව්ව ගමන් එක කණ්ඩායමක් කිව්වා, අපි ෙපොංගු තමිල් නාඩගම් ආෙයමත් නටන්න ෙදන්ෙන් නැහැ කියලා. තවත් අය කිව්වා, අපි උසාවි යනවා කියලා. තවත් අය ෙම් සම්බන්ධෙයන් විවිධාකාරෙයන් ෙම් ආණ්ඩුවට පහර ගැහුවා. නමුත් ෙම් පහර ගහන අය පසු ගිය ආණ්ඩුෙව් ඇමතිකම් දරන ෙකොට, මන්තීකම් දරන ෙකොට, පසු ගිය ආණ්ඩුව අවුරුදු අටක්, නවයක් ෙම් රට පාලනය කරලා ඒ අයත් ෙම් විධියටම කටයුතු කරන ෙකොට -උදාහරණයක් හැටියට ෙදමළ ඩයස්ෙපෝරාව එක්ක සාකච්ඡා කරන ෙකොට - ඒ ගැන ෙමොකුත් කථා කෙළේ නැහැ.

Now, I have here with me a news item that appeared on the "dailymirror.lk" website on 15th August, 2012 captioned “Tamil Diaspora delegation meets Gota”, which states, I quote:

“Former LTTE Chief Arms procurer Kumaran Pathmanathan (KP) said a group of 22 members of the Tamil diaspora from Canada, Australia and five European Countries had visited Sri Lanka last week and held talks with Defence Secretary Gotabaya Rajapaksa in Colombo.”

ඒ විතරක් ෙනොෙවයි, මම ෙම් කාරණා ටිකත් ඉක්මනින් කියවන්නම්. The “LankaTruth” website published a news item titled “Here’s the relationship between Mahinda & Tamil diaspora” on 17th December, 2014, which states, I quote:

“It is revealed that Mr. Mahinda Rajapaksa, who has again started saying there is an international conspiracy to take him to the electric chair, has very close relationships with the Tamil diaspora.

It is revealed through internet that there had been a meeting between Mr. Mahinda Rajapaksa and a group including Dharmalingam Lokeshwaran, a former activist of the LTTE and a person who has had special knowledge regarding collecting money for the LTTE.”

There is not only the news item, but here are the pictures. There are pictures of the former President, Mahinda Rajapaksa, basically embracing the Tamil diaspora. I am not complaining about it. Here, are also pictures of the former President, Mahinda Rajapaksa, posing with very pretty girls from the Tamil diaspora and their family members.

මූලාසනාරූඪ ගරු මන්තීතුමියනි, ෙක්පීෙග් වුවමනාවට එදා ඩයස්ෙපෝරාව එක්ක කථා කරලා, එල්ටීටීඊ සල්ලි ළඟ තියාෙගන ඉන්න පධානීන් ලංකාවට ෙගනැත්, ෙම් ආකාරයට පින්තූර අරෙගන, පිළි අරෙගන කටයුතු කරන ෙකොට ෙම් අය නිහඬව සිටියා. ෙම් අය ඇවිත් තිෙයන්ෙනත් ලංකාෙව් මුදලින්. ෙම් අද කෑ ගහන අය එදා මීෙයෝ ගිලපු පුංචි පූස් පැටව් වාෙග් වලිගය පිටුපස්ෙසේ ගහෙගන බුදියාගත්තා. විපක්ෂෙය් විතරක් ෙනොෙවයි, ආණ්ඩු පක්ෂෙය්ත් ඉන්නවා ඒ අය. එදා ආණ්ඩුෙව් ඇමතිකම් අරෙගන ඔවුන් නිහඬව හිටියා. කවුරුවත් වචනයකින්වත් කිව්ෙව් නැහැ, "ෙම්වා වැරැදියි" කියලා. නමුත්, අද අප ෙම් ෙගන්වන්ෙන් එල්ටීටීඊ සංවිධානෙය් සල්ලි එකතු කරන අය ෙනොෙවයි; එල්ටීටීඊ සංවිධානෙය් ෙලොකු ෙලොක්කන් ෙනොෙවයි. ඔය එල්ටීටීඊ සංවිධානය ෙවනුෙවන් අද ෙපනී සිටින විමල් වීරවංශෙග් මිතෙයක් ෙවන්න ඇති, ෙඩොනල්ඩ් ඥාණෙකෝන් වාෙග්. ෙමොකද, අර කිව්වා වාෙග්, ෙපෞද්ගලික ඊ-ෙම්ල් එකක් තිෙබන්න බැහැ ෙන්, එයා අඳුරන්ෙන් නැත්නම්. ඔන්න එවැනි අය ෙකොටසක් ඉන්නවා. නමුත්, අද අප සාකච්ඡා කරන්ෙන් එවැනි අය සමඟ ෙනොෙවයි.

උගත් පාඩම් හා පතිසන්ධානය පිළිබඳ වූ ජනාධිපති ෙකොමිෂන් සභා වාර්තාෙව් කියපු විධියටම, ෙම් රට ඉදිරියට ෙගන යන්න නම් අප ෙම් හැම ෙකෙනක්ම දිනා ගන්න ඕනෑ. අප සාකච්ඡා තුන හතරක් පවත්වලා තිෙබනවා. නමුත්, ඒ එක සාකච්ඡාවකදීවත් අප ෙද්ශපාලන විසඳුමක් ගැන, එෙහම නැත්නම් යුද අපරාධ ගැනවත් ෙනොෙවයි කථා කෙළේ.

නව ශී ලංකාවක් නිර්මාණය කිරීෙම් අෙප් කටයුත්තට ඒ අයෙග් දායකත්වය ලබා ගන්ෙන් ෙකොෙහොමද කියලායි සාකච්ඡා කෙළේ. ඒ අනුව ෙම් වන විටත් ඉතාම පසිද්ධ ෛවදɕවරු පිරිසක් -සිංහල, ෙදමළ, මුස්ලිම් කීප ෙදෙනකුත් ඒ අතර ඉන්නවා.- කැමැත්ත පකාශ කර තිෙබනවා ලංකාවට ඇවිත් ෙප්දුරු තුඩුෙව් සිට ෙදවුන්දර තුඩුව දක්වා සිංහල, ෙදමළ, මුස්ලිම් පෙද්ශවලට ගිහින් ෛවදɕ සායන තියන්න. ඒෙක් වරදක් තිෙබනවාද?

කරු ජයසූරිය ඇමතිතුමා කිව්වා වාෙග්, ඉතාම ඉහළ ෙපෙළේ, ෙඩොලර් ෙකෝටිපති වɕාපාරිකයන් ඉන්නවා. ඒ අෙප් රෙට් අය. ඒ අය ගැන අප ආඩම්බර ෙවන්න ඕනෑ. ඒ අය ලංකාවට ඇවිත් ලංකාෙව් ආෙයෝජන අවස්ථා ලබා ගන්නවා නම්, ඒ අවස්ථාෙවන් උතුෙර් ඉන්න තරුණයන්ට විතරක් ෙනොෙවයි, දකුෙණ් ඉන්න තරුණයන්ටත් රැකියා අවස්ථා ඇති ෙවනවා කියලා අප කියන්න ඕනෑ. ඒ වාෙග් තව විවිධ දක්ෂතා ඇති අය ඉන්නවා. සින්දු කියන්න පුළුවන් ගායකයන් ඉන්නවා, ලංකාවට එන්න කැමැති. ෙපොත් ලියන්න පුළුවන් අය ඉන්නවා, ලංකාවට ඇවිත් ඒ කාලෙය් සාහිතɕ උෙළලක් තියන්න කැමැති. රජවරුන්ට, කුමාරයන්ට, ජනාධිපතිවරුන්ට උයන ලාංකික ෙකෝකිවරු ඉන්නවා, ෙමහාට ඇවිත් food festivals තියන්න කැමැති. මූලාසනාරූඪ ගරු මන්තීතුමියනි, ඒෙක් ඇති වරද ෙමොකක්ද?

447 448

2015 ජුනි 25

දැන් කියනවා, එල්ටීටීඊ සංවිධානය හිස ඔසවනවා ලු. නමුත්, මම ඊෙය් කිව්වා වාෙග්, ෙම් වාර්තාවත් කියන්ෙන් 2014 වර්ෂය ගැනයි. ඒෙකන් මා කියන්ෙන් නැහැ, එල්ටීටීඊ සංවිධානෙය් සල්ලි එකතු කරන අය නැත්තටම නැහැ කියලා. ඒ වාෙග් අය ඉන්නවා. ෙම් වාර්තාෙව් තිෙබන්ෙන් රාජපක්ෂෙග් කාලය ගැනයි. නමුත්, මෙග් විශ්වාසයක් තිෙබනවා ෙම් මාස පහට ඒවා තවත් අඩු ෙවයි කියලා. ඒ වාර්තාව අපි එන අවුරුද්ෙද් බලමු.

අද ඔබතුමන්ලා ෙම් විධියට කෑ ගහනවා. නමුත්, මම දන්නවා අජිත් නිවාඩ් කබ්රාල් පසු ගිය අවුරුද්ෙද් සැප්තැම්බර්, ඔක්ෙතෝබර් මාසවල ෙකොන්සවටිව් පක්ෂෙය් වාර්ෂික සම්ෙම්ලනයට සහභාගී ෙවන්න ගිහින්, ඉන් පසුව ලන්ඩන්වලදී තවමත් ඊළාම් මතය අත් ෙනොහැරපු ඩයස්ෙපෝරා කණ්ඩායම් එක්ක සාකච්ඡා කළ බව.

ලංකාවට ඇවිල්ලා ෙක්පී එක්කත් සාකච්ඡා කළා. ෙම් ඩයස්ෙපෝරා එදා කා එක්කද සාකච්ඡා කරන්ෙන්, කා එක්කද සාකච්ඡා ෙනොකරන්ෙන් කියලා තීන්දු කෙළේ කවුද? ඒ ෙවන කවුරුවත් ෙනොෙවයි. ෙකොටි සංවිධානෙය් ජාතɕන්තර මුදල් භාරව හිටපු ෙක්පීයි. එයා තමයි ආණ්ඩුවට කිව්ෙව්, ෙමයත් එක්ක කථා කරන්න, ෙමයත් එක්ක කථා කරන්න එපා කියලා. අන්තිමට ඒෙක් පතිඵලයක් හැටියට යුෙරෝපීය සංගමෙය් ෙකොටි තහනමවත් ආරක්ෂා කර ගන්න බැරි වුණා. ගරු ජී.එල්. පීරිස් මැතිතුමනි, හිටපු ඇමතිතුමා හැටියට ඔබතුමාත් ෙම්කට වග කියන්න ඕනෑ බව මා කනගාටුෙවන් කියනවා. මා 2006 දී ෙබොෙහොම අමාරුෙවන් රටක් රටක් ගාෙන් ගිහිල්ලා අන්තිමට ඇෙමරිකා එක්සත් ජනපදෙය් රාජɕ ෙදපාර්තෙම්න්තුෙව්ත් සහෙයෝගය ඇතිව යුෙරෝපීය සංගමෙයන් ඒ ලබා ගත්ත ඒකමතික තහනම ඒ අය ඉවත් කළා, ගිය අවුරුද්ෙද් අන්තිෙම්දී. නමුත් අෙප් ෙම් ආණ්ඩුව ඇවිල්ලා තමයි - [බාධා කිරීමක්] හරි. නමුත් ඒකට ඔබතුමන්ලා වැඩි අවධානයක් ෙයොමු කෙළේ නැහැ. ඔබතුමන්ලා එෙහම ෙදයක් වනවාද කියන එකවත් දැන ෙගන හිටියාද කියලා මා දන්ෙන් නැහැ. [බාධා කිරීමක්] සමාෙවන්න. ඇපෑලක් දමලා තිබුෙණ් නැහැ. එෙහම එකක් තිබුෙණ් නැහැ. ඒ ඔක්ෙකෝම කෙළේ අපි. මට මතකයි, අපි කෑ ගැහුවා ඒ ෙවලාෙව්. ඊට පස්ෙසේ, මා විෙද්ශ ඇමතිවරයා වශෙයන් පළමුෙවන්ම ගිෙය් නවදිල්ලියට. ෙදවනුව ගිෙය් යුෙරෝපීය සංගමෙය් කාර්යාලයට, Brusselsවලට. ඇමතිවරයා ෙවලා පළමුවැනි සති තුන ඇතුළත ගිහිල්ලා GSP Plus සහනය නැවත ලබා ගන්නත්, ධීවර සහනය නැවත ලබා ගන්නත්, ෙකොටි තහනම යළි පනවන්නත් කටයුතු කළ නිසා තමයි, මාර්තු මාසය වන ෙකොට යළි තහනම් කර ගන්නට පුළුවන් වුෙණ්. ඇත්තටම කියනවා නම්- [බාධා කිරීමක්] අපට නම් එෙහම ෙදයක් කිව්ෙව් නැහැ. ෙකෙසේ ෙවතත්, ඒ ෙකොටි තහනම ඉවත් කර දීමත් එක්තරා විධියකට ආණ්ඩුකම වɕවස්ථාෙව් හයවන සංෙශෝධනය උල්ලංඝනය කිරීමක්.

It amounts to high treason. One day even you might have to be tried for high treason, God forbid! This is negligence on the part of the Foreign Ministry. I am just expressing an idea, but it was a very, very serious flaw or a serious mishap as far as our foreign policy is concerned.

Madam, I explained to the House yesterday, in response to a Questions raised by the Hon. Leader of the Opposition, that the US State Department Report titled, “Country Reports on Terrorism and Patterns of Global Terrorism” that was released this month is not something new. It has followed other Reports of this nature, which the US State Department is bound by law to submit annually, and has been submitting since 2004. I also explained that the Report that was issued recently was the

Report covering activity in 2014, which fell under the purview of the previous administration.

This statement, Madam, was part of a general description of where the LTTE would receive its external funding in the past, and is not an indicator of current activity. But, I must also say that our Government is not sufficiently "blue-eyed" to claim that such funding activities have ceased completely since our Government has come into power. What the Report does say about current activities, however, is that there are still some LTTE supporters, strength unknown, 13 of who were arrested last year, and that their financial networks continued to operate throughout the year 2014.

This information is well known to most Sri Lankans. Further, it is very well known to my predecessor, the Hon. Prof. G.L. Peiris who has called for this Debate today. He knows very well that the Report pertains to the period under his purview. He also knows very well, having held the post of Foreign Minister of the previous Government, the concerns that the international community had at the time regarding Sri Lanka: the drifting of this nation towards authoritarianism, the disregard for the grievances of the Tamil population in the North, the breakdown of law and order, the clamping down on any expressions of concern or dissent, the narrowing of space for civil society, the tendency to brand as terrorists even those who merely expressed concerns regarding the welfare of the people. He also knows of the increase of terror and fear of Sri Lankan people under the activities of the State, including the terror created by radical groups like the BBS, who, as I claimed even then, were funded by the Ministry of Defence of Sri Lanka.

He knows all this very well. He also knew that these concerns had given rise to serious concerns among the international community and the local public as well regarding the real possibilities of the LTTE regrouping; not only the LTTE, but even the possibility of sensible, rational and responsible citizens of this country being pushed to contemplate violence as a means of having their concerns addressed. In fact, I sincerely believe that had your Government continued, had the Presidency not been rescued in January, the LTTE would have regrouped and resurfaced much earlier because of your short-sighted triumphant policies which may have created many more young Prabhakarans for the future.

Madam, while creating fear and paranoia among our citizens, and giving the impression of an effective strong-man approach to defeating terrorism, the previous Government gave pardon to the very man who took control of the LTTE after Prabhakaran’s death - KP. Not only that, but KP was allowed to live in Kilinochchi and take charge of an NGO handling refugees and victims and, as I just mentioned, even the coordination of the diaspora.

449 450

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව

This is a man who is believed to possess information on the LTTE’s vast international assets. So, why was the Government protecting him? Moreover, why was the Government protecting him when previous US State Department reports noted that the LTTE financial networks continued to function?

In fact, the same Report in 2013 actually said that these were functioning very effectively even in that year and instead of questioning or taking action against KP, you actually made him a close buddy of the First Family. Our Government, on the other hand, banned KP from leaving the country in February and is investigating his activities. So, we may freeze once and for all, the financial networks of the LTTE.

Madam, our Government is continuing to intensify relations with our intelligence networks abroad and has increased access to real time information from these sources about the activities of the LTTE. In fact, the Statement issued by the State Minister of Defence, the Hon. Ruwan Wijayawardhana has very rightly rejected the statements made by some Opposition politicians and former Defence Secretary, Gotabhaya Rajapaksa, on the country’s national security. He notes that not only are previous security measures being sustained, but that under the present Leadership, the Tri-forces and Intelligence Services are active and effective as never before.

Today, the Government is renewing its relations with the international community. Today, we are engaging with our bilateral partners as opposed to just lecturing to them and talking with them, which the previous Government used to do. We engage in conversations with them in a rational manner on what our real concerns are and we are able to take steps to build confidence, so that we can share information, share intelligence and work together to combat terrorism.

The Opposition is now keen to benefit from public US intelligence reports about the LTTE, but we are disappointed then that they continue to talk along the lines of “international conspiracies.” This Government has always taken the line that we will not allow - as I have said several times before here - an international investigation..

However, we have always maintained that we will use a credible, local mechanism with international technical assistance in keeping with the mandate His Excellency President Maithipala Sirisena received on the 8th of January. If you actually look at the 100-Day Manifesto, Item 93 clearly states that we will establish a domestic mechanism in order to meet the allegations of human rights violations and even perhaps allegations of war crimes.

Establishing a credible mechanism to deal with the allegation of serious human rights violations during the latter part of the conflict, is something that the previous Government failed to do, which opened the doors to international scrutiny, and has prevented the Sri Lankan people from being able to achieve closure and move on from its violent past. This only gave the international community an opening to interfere with the domestic affairs of our country. In fact, failures of the previous Government investigations to achieve credibility and plausibility, prompted the creation of the OHCHR investigation on Sri Lanka in a Resolution adopted in March, 2014. So, it is actually the previous Government’s failures to establish legitimacy that is responsible. It is the timely entrance of a new Government in January this year, with a firm commitment to a credible domestic mechanism, that has enabled us to taper the call for an international investigation imposed on Sri Lanka by the international community.

Madam Chair, defending the sovereignty and territorial integrity of the country is essential to the foreign policy of our nation. As this House is aware, sovereignty carries with it great responsibility, which involves duties towards the country’s citizens. When a Government fails to discharge such duties, external intervention of an unwelcome nature is difficult to prevent.

The previous Government, regrettably, failed to pursue the path of domestic peace-building and by refusing to address issues of concern locally, the Government alienated communities within the country as well as Sri Lanka’s international partners. This is what led to our nation becoming the subject of successive Resolutions in Geneva.

Madam, it is the previous Government, by opening up this nation to international ignominy through its failures in fulfilling duties it owed to its people, that Sri Lanka was made vulnerable to intrusive external intervention, placing the nation’s sovereignty and territorial integrity at risk.

Let me also respond to the Hon. (Prof.) G.L. Peiris’ next allegation that by our domestic mechanism benefitting from international expertise, it effectively becomes an “international investigation”. Let me remind this House that accepting and using international expertise is something even the Rajapaksa Government loved to do at great expense at that time to our country . Under the Rajapaksa regime, the Central Bank - ගරු (මහාචාර්ය) ජී. එල්. පීරිස් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு (ேபராசிாியர்) ஜீ.எல். பீாிஸ்) (The Hon. (Prof.) G.L. Peiris) I did not say that. I did not object to international expertise. That is wrong. I asked in what - [Interruption.].

451 452

[ගරු මංගල සමරවීර මහතා]

2015 ජුනි 25

ගරු මංගල සමරවීර මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு மங்கள சமரᾪர) (The Hon. Mangala Samaraweera) When you read between the lines, you were basically saying that by having international expertise, it may become an “international investigation”. ගරු (මහාචාර්ය) ජී. එල්. පීරිස් මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு (ேபராசிாியர்) ஜீ.எல். பீாிஸ்) (The Hon. (Prof.) G.L. Peiris) I wanted to ask what are the limits - [Interruption.] I did not object to international investigation. ගරු මංගල සමරවීර මහතා (மாண்ᾗமிகு மங்கள சமரᾪர) (The Hon. Mangala Samaraweera) I would also like to remind this House that under the last regime - I know that you were usually unaware of the fact that many of these funds came from the Central Bank and not from the Foreign Ministry - the Central Bank and other Government institutions spent Rs. 2 billion on international PR firms to enhance the poor reputation they created for themselves. This included firms such as Thompson Advisory Group, Beltway Government Strategies and Liberty International Group, all of which, I believe, were hired on the whims and fancies of - I do not know what you call him - the Member of Parliament, who monitored even your activities. In fact, I know that sometimes even your conversations were taped and sent to his room for him to listen. Further, on 17th July, 2014, President Rajapaksa announced that the panel of international legal experts, who were to advise his Commission on Disappearances, would also investigate abuses committed during the final stages of Sri Lanka’s civil war. He, therefore, publicly noted that international experts would be advising him on violations of international humanitarian law and international human rights law.

International legal advisers and a former international judge were appointed by President Rajapaksa for the purpose of soliciting “international expertise.” Documents note that just for seven months, more than Rs.135 million of tax-payers' money had been paid out to them as well as others who were connected with this exercise. In fact, some of these experts were paid nearly Sterling Pounds 55,000 a month for their activities.

Madam Chair, the Rajapaksa Government hired international expertise at the expense of the tax-payer instead of receiving it out of goodwill of our friends. Our close partners and friends in the international community who helped us fight the LTTE, drifted away from us after May, 2009. It is important to ask the previous Government why this was allowed to happen.

Why is it that these very countries that helped us fight the LTTE, later initiated action against Sri Lanka in the Human Rights Council in Geneva? Why did the previous Government allow such a situation to develop and allow

the country’s image to sink to the lowest depths imaginable? I hope, Madam Chair, even if my predecessor cannot answer these questions now, he should, for his own benefit, search his conscience as to why he allowed some of these things to happen.

In my earlier incarnation as Foreign Minister, I expended great effort to list the LTTE - as I mentioned earlier - as a terrorist organization by the EU in 2006. That, Madam Chair, was not achieved alone. The unanimity needed to arrive at such a decision was achieved with some help from our friends in the US State Department then. Friendly and responsible foreign governments who stood with us to combat terrorism assisted us. They investigated the LTTE and shared that information with the members of the EU.

We must, in the interest of national security, raise the question as to why the previous Government allowed that listing, which was achieved with such effort with the support of the international community, to be annulled last year on the 16th of October by the General Court of the European Union. It is pertinent to have an inquiry on why such an important matter with serious implications for national security was not taken seriously. Why was there no timely intervention by the Government at the time to prevent the delisting? Also, there were remarks relating to the High Commissioner for Human Rights at the opening of the currently ongoing 29th Session of the Human Rights Council in Geneva. The High Commissioner did something on the 15th of June this year, which the Council had not seen done in a long time with reference to Sri Lanka.

Madam Chair, he reflected in his remarks the opportunity that has opened up in Sri Lanka - the renewed hope for democracy and the rule of law - with the passage of the 19th Amendment to the Constitution. This is something which this House can take pride in collectively, because we all voted for it collectively, and work together to give effect to the provisions of that Amendment.

Madam, having informed the Human Rights Council of the renewed hope for democracy and the rule of law in Sri Lanka, what the High Commissioner for Human Rights went on to say is that his office will remain engaged in discussions with Sri Lankan authorities on “the need for transparent and inclusive processes to develop credible processes to develop credible mechanisms for accountability and reconciliation ahead of my report to the September Session”. The High Commissioner is merely reflecting on our consensual approach for broad consultations with all political parities, civil society and above all, victims and their families to take place in the lead up to September before establishing a domestic mechanism. We will conduct consultations to ensure full national support and ownership of processes. This Government fully recognizes the importance of consultations and transparency.

453 454

පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව

Madam Chair, I wish to point out here that it was the complete lack of any form of consultations with civil society groups or political parties or victims by the previous regime that resulted in the setting up of flawed processes and programmes that contributed in large measure to the loss of credibility in whatever the previous Government undertook to do, both in the eyes of the local public as well as the international community. Not even were the views of public officials given any consideration at the time, except for the views of those who said that all that the previous Government was doing was well and good, and wise. Not only that, even the wise counsel given by the Commission of Inquiry on Lessons Learnt and Reconciliation, a Commission appointed by President Rajapaksa , itself was ignored.

All this contributed to Sri Lanka losing the best opportunities it had after the end of 30 years of conflict to rebuild its institutions, restore democracy, rule of law and good governance practices, heal hearts and minds, enhance the capacities and skills of its human resources - the administrative and other services including the foreign and judicial services.

The Hon. (Prof.) Peiris has selectively singled out the remarks of Senator Leahy pertaining to the establishment of a domestic mechanism. I would like to ask the Hon. Member of Parliament, whether he recalls the nature of statements that were made with reference to Sri Lanka by foreign policy experts during the time he was the Minister of External Affairs and ask whether there was anything complimentary being said? Senator Leahy compliments Sri Lanka for its recent achievements , some of which are: the passage of the 19th Amendment to the Constitution, the inclusion of the Right to Information in the Constitution as a fundamental right, the revival of relations with the United Nations, the decision to revive accountability for human rights violations, the decision to pursue the twin agenda of reconciliation and development, the return of land to its original owners, reaffirmation of media freedom, re-establishment of judicial independence, and commitment to fighting corruption.

In the recent 2015 Elections, which had the highest-ever turnout and was an overwhelming victory, the President made very clear, the need to establish a national independent judicial mechanism. This is expressed clearly in his 100-Day Manifesto, under Item 93, which states, I quote:

"Since Sri Lanka is not a signatory to the Rome Statute regarding international jurisdiction with regard to war crimes, ensuring justice with regard to such matters will be the business of national independent judicial mechanisms."

Thus, it has been mandated by this Government and the people of Sri Lanka also.

In conclusion, I would like to say, Madam Chair, that Sri Lanka has had a long tradition of respect for the rule of law and accountability at all levels and in relation to all matters of public life, including administrative and financial matters. We saw a general deterioration of these practices in the years of conflict. It is in our country’s long-term interest and in the interest of future generations that we must restore these practices of accountability and not take cover behind imagined threats to national security. If we continue the practice of the last Government of conjuring up threats to national security and clamping down on civil liberties for short-term electoral gain without actually engaging with the public and our international partners to address real threats as opposed to imagined threats, then we will surely jeopardize national security and place this country’s future in peril.

Thank you. එකල්හි ෙව්ලාව අ. භා. 6.30 වූෙයන් මූලාසනාරූඪ ගරු මන්තීතුමිය විසින් පශ්නය ෙනොවිමසා පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව කල් තබන ලදී. පාර්ලිෙම්න්තුව ඊට අනුකූලව, 2015 ජුනි මස 26වන සිකුරාදා අ. භා. 1.30 වන ෙතක් කල් ගිෙය්ය. அப்ெபாᾨᾐ, பி. ப. 6.30 மணியாகிவிடேவ, தைலைமதாங்கும் உᾠப்பினர் அவர்கள் வினா விᾌக்காமேலேய பாராᾦமன்றத்ைத ஒத்திைவத்தார். அதன்பᾊ பாராᾦமன்றம், 2015 ᾝன் 26, ெவள்ளிக்கிழைம பி. ப. 1.30 மணிவைர ஒத்திைவக்கப்பட்டᾐ

It being 6.30 p.m., THE PRESIDING MEMBER adjourned Parliament without Question put. Adjourned accordingly until 1.30 p.m. on Friday, 26th June, 2015.

[ගරු මංගල සමරවීර මහතා]

සැ.යු. ෙමම වාර්තාෙව් අවසාන මුදණය සඳහා ස්වකීය නිවැරදි කළ යුතු තැන් දක්වනු රිසි මන්තීන් මින් පිටපතක් ෙගන නිවැරදි කළ යුතු ආකාරය එහි පැහැදිලිව ලකුණු ෙකොට, පිටපත ලැබී ෙදසතියක් ෙනොඉක්මවා හැන්සාඩ් සංස්කාරක ෙවත ලැෙබන ෙසේ එවිය යුතුය.
